 &lt;script async=&quot;true&quot; src=&quot;https://www.instagram.com/embed.js&quot;&gt;&lt;/script&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;span&gt;  &lt;/span&gt;" data-reactid="26"><span>  <script async="true" src="https://www.instagram.com/embed.js"></script> </span><span>  </span></p><span data-reactid="27"></span><div class="canvas-tweet canvas-atom Ov(a) W(100%)" data-type="tweet" data-reactid="28"><blockquote class="twitter-tweet"> <p>There is a 10 year old black boy,Bryce, in America who has been hit with an aggravated assault charge via Dodgeball. <br><br>All because the white boys mother, who knew about his illness, didnt specify to the school that her child should not be involved with that type of sport</p> LaShanna (@87Halfpint) <a href="https://twitter.com/87Halfpint/status/1155517939312988161?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">July 28, 2019</a> </blockquote></div><p class="canvas-atom canvas-text Mb(1.0em) Mb(0)--sm Mt(0.8em)--sm" type="text" content="Some seem to imply that the incident appears to fit into a larger pattern  of what various studies have found to be disproportionate punishments between black and white children in America." data-reactid="29">Some seem to imply that the incident appears to fit into a larger pattern  of what various studies have found to be disproportionate punishments between black and white children in America.</p><p class="canvas-atom canvas-text Mb(1.0em) Mb(0)--sm Mt(0.8em)--sm" type="text" content="A 2018 report by the watchdog Government Accountability Group found that black students in grades K-12 are far more likely to be disciplined at school  whether through suspension or referral to law enforcement  than kids of other races. Further, noted the&amp;nbsp;&lt;a href=&quot;https://www.nytimes.com/2017/09/25/opinion/black-students-little-rock-punishment.html&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow noopener&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;New York Times &lt;/a&gt;in 2017, during the 2012 school year, black students [in Arkansas] were suspended five times as often as whites were, and little has changed since then. The racial discipline gap is not restricted to Arkansas, or to the South. The same report finds that several Northern states, including Illinois, Michigan and Wisconsin, rank above Arkansas in the black-white suspension gap. Another&amp;nbsp;&lt;a href=&quot;https://www.brookings.edu/research/2017-brown-center-report-part-iii-race-and-school-suspensions/&quot; title rel=&quot;nofollow noopener&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;study&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp; from the Brookings Institution, looking at California schools  found evidence of the gap despite statewide efforts to reduce suspensions." data-reactid="30">A 2018 report by the watchdog Government Accountability Group found that black students in grades K-12 are far more likely to be disciplined at school  whether through suspension or referral to law enforcement  than kids of other races. Further, noted the&nbsp;<a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2017/09/25/opinion/black-students-little-rock-punishment.html" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">New York Times </a>in 2017, during the 2012 school year, black students [in Arkansas] were suspended five times as often as whites were, and little has changed since then. The racial discipline gap is not restricted to Arkansas, or to the South. The same report finds that several Northern states, including Illinois, Michigan and Wisconsin, rank above Arkansas in the black-white suspension gap. Another&nbsp;<a href="https://www.brookings.edu/research/2017-brown-center-report-part-iii-race-and-school-suspensions/" title rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">study</a>&nbsp; from the Brookings Institution, looking at California schools  found evidence of the gap despite statewide efforts to reduce suspensions.</p><p class="canvas-atom canvas-text Mb(1.0em) Mb(0)--sm Mt(0.8em)--sm" type="text" content="In the meantime, Lindley has created a&amp;nbsp;&lt;a href=&quot;https://www.facebook.com/donate/347175299538463/&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow noopener&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;fundraiser &lt;/a&gt;to assist her with Bryces legal fees and they are set to appear in juvenile court on Aug. 1st.
